# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:


Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server audit logging implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **13 core Go source files** in `kubernetes/kubernetes` that implement API server audit logging, along with **20 key symbols** (functions and types) that drive the functionality.

### Key Components:

1. **Audit Event Creation & Context Management**
   - `WithAuditInit` - initializes audit context and Audit-ID
   - `WithAuditContext` - manages audit context throughout request lifecycle
   - `LogRequestMetadata`, `LogRequestObject`, `LogResponseObject` - populate audit events with request/response data

2. **Audit Policy Evaluation**
   - `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` - creates policy evaluator from YAML/JSON policy files
   - `EvaluatePolicyRule` - matches requests against policy rules based on users, groups, verbs, resources, etc.

3. **Audit Event Processing Pipeline**
   - `WithAudit` - main decorator that orchestrates audit event creation and dispatch at different request stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic)
   - `processAuditEvent` - sends events to audit backends

4. **Backend Dispatch System**
   - **Union Backend** - combines multiple backends for parallel event delivery
   - **File Backend** - writes to JSON/legacy text format files with rotation
   - **Webhook Backend** - sends events to HTTP endpoints with exponential backoff retry
   - **Buffered Backend** - batches events asynchronously with configurable buffering, batching, and rate limiting

5. **Audit Truncation**
   - Automatically removes RequestObject and ResponseObject when events exceed MaxEventSize
   - Preserves event metadata to maintain auditability

management. This is paired with `WithAuditContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go`, which creates the core `AuditContext` structure that holds the audit event being captured and the evaluated policy configuration.\\n\\nThe `AuditContext` is stored in the request context and provides thread-safe access to audit annotations via `AddAuditAnnotation` and related methods. The `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go` file contains critical functions for populating audit events: `LogRequestMetadata` captures HTTP request information (URI, user, source IPs, verb), `LogRequestObject` serializes the request body, and `LogResponseObject` captures response data.\\n\\n## Audit Policy Evaluation\\nThe audit policy evaluation component in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go` implements the `PolicyRuleEvaluator` interface (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/evaluator.go`). The `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` function creates an evaluator from a policy loaded by `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go`, which parses audit policy YAML/JSON files. The `EvaluatePolicyRule` method matches incoming requests against policy rules by checking users, groups, verbs, namespaces, resources, and non-resource URLs, returning a `RequestAuditConfig` that specifies the audit level, omit stages, and whether to omit managed fields.\\n\\n## Audit Event Processing and Dispatch\\nThe core request handler decorator `WithAudit` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go` orchestrates the full audit flow. The function tracks response status codes and latencies through an `auditResponseWriter` decorator that implements HTTP response writer interception.\\n\\n## Audit Backend Architecture\\nAudit events flow through a dispatch system defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go`. The `Union` function creates a composite backend that sends events to multiple backends in sequence. Three main backend implementations are provided:\\n\\n1. **File Logging Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go`): The `NewBackend` function creates a file-based backend that writes audit events in JSON or legacy text format to an I/O writer (typically a rotating file via lumberjack).\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go`): The `NewBackend` function creates an HTTP webhook backend that batches events and sends them to an external service via POST requests. It implements exponential backoff retry logic for resilience.\\n\\n3. **Buffered/Batching Backend** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go`): The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend to batch events asynchronously. It supports configurable buffer sizes, batch sizes, batching intervals, and throttling (QPS-based rate limiting) for controlling the flow of events to the delegate backend.\\n\\n## Audit Event Truncation\\nThe truncate backend in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go` handles truncation of large request and response bodies. The `NewBackend` function wraps a delegate backend and implements the `ProcessEvents` method to calculate event sizes and automatically remove RequestObject and ResponseObject fields when events exceed the configured `MaxEventSize`, while still preserving metadata. It also batches events to respect `MaxBatchSize` limits and delegates to the underlying backend.\\n\\n## Configuration and Integration\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go` file orchestrates the complete audit system setup. The `NewAuditOptions` function creates audit configuration objects for log and webhook backends with default settings. The `ApplyTo` method integrates audit into the server by: (1) loading the audit policy file, (2) creating log and webhook backends, (3) wrapping backends with truncation and buffering configurations, and (4) registering the combined backend and policy evaluator in the server configuration.\\n\\nThe main request handler chain in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` applies the audit filters in order: `WithAuditInit` first to initialize the context and Audit-ID, then `WithAudit` to handle the core audit logging with policy evaluation and event dispatch. This ensures that audit events are created from the initial request through response completion, with proper handling of long-running requests that may emit multiple audit events at different stages.\"\n}\n",
